AN ICELANDIC PRIMER

With Grammar, Notes, and Glossary

By Henry Sweet, M.A.

SECOND EDITION

1895



PREFACE

The want of a short and easy introduction to the study of
Icelandic has been felt for a long time--in fact, from the very
beginning of that study in England.  The _Icelandic Reader_,
edited by Messrs.  Vigfusson and Powell, in the Clarendon Press
Series, is a most valuable book, which ought to be in the hands
of every student; but it still leaves room for an elementary
primer.  As the engagements of the editors of the Reader would
have made it impossible for them to undertake such a work for
some years to come, they raised no objections to my proposal to
undertake it myself.  Meanwhile, I found the task was a more
formidable one than I had anticipated, and accordingly, before
definitely committing myself to it, I made one final attempt to
induce Messrs.  Vigfusson and Powell to take it off my hands; but
they very kindly encouraged me to proceed with it; and as I
myself thought that an Icelandic primer, on the lines of my
Anglo-Saxon one, might perhaps be the means of inducing some
students of Old English to take up Icelandic as well, I
determined to go on.

In the spelling I have not thought it necessary to adhere
strictly to that adopted in the Reader, for the editors have
themselves deviated from it in their _Corpus Poeticum Boreale_,
in the way of separating _脟芦_ from _脙露_, etc.  My own principle has
been to deviate as little as possible from the traditional
spelling followed in normalized texts.  There is, indeed, no
practical gain for the beginner in writing _t脛芦me_ for _t脛芦mi_,
discarding _脙掳_, etc., although these changes certainly bring us
nearer the oldest MSS., and cannot be dispensed with in
scientific works.  The essential thing for the beginner is to
have _regular_ forms presented to him, to the exclusion, as far
as possible, of isolated archaisms, and to have the defective
distinctions of the MSS. supplemented by diacritics.  I have not
hesitated to substitute (脗炉) for (脗麓) as the mark of length; the
latter ought in my opinion to be used exclusively--in Icelandic
as well as in Old English and Old Irish--to represent the actual
accents of the MSS.

In the grammar I have to acknowledge my great obligations to
Noreen's _Altisl脙陇ndische Grammatik_, which is by far the best
Icelandic grammar that has yet appeared--at least from that
narrow point of view which ignores syntax, and concentrates
itself on phonology and inflections.

The texts are intended to be as easy, interesting, and
representative as possible.  With such a language, and such a
master of it as Snorri to choose from, this combination is not
difficult to realise.  The beginner is indeed to be envied who
makes his first acquaintance with the splendid mythological tales
of the North, told in an absolutely perfect style.  As the death
of Olaf Tryggvason is given in the Reader only from the longer
recension of the Heimskringla, I have been able to give the
shorter text, which is admirably suited for the purposes of this
book.  The story of Au脙掳un is not only a beautiful one in itself,
but, together with the preceding piece, gives a vivid idea of the
Norse ideal of the kingly character, which was the foundation of
their whole political system.  As the Reader does not include
poetry (except incidentally), I have added one of the finest of
the Eddaic poems, which is at the same time freest from obscurity
and corruption--the song of Thor's quest of his hammer.

In the glossary I have ventured to deviate from the very
inconvenient Scandinavian arrangement, which puts _脙戮_, _脙娄_, _脜聯_,
right at the end of the alphabet.

I have to acknowledge the great help I have had in preparing the
texts and the glossary from Wimmer's _Oldnordisk L脙娄sebog_, which
I consider to be, on the whole, the best reading-book that exists
in any language.  So excellent is Wimmer's selection of texts,
that it was impossible for me to do otherwise than follow him in
nearly every case.

In conclusion, it is almost superfluous to say that this book
makes no pretension to originality of any kind.  If it
contributes towards restoring to Englishmen that precious
heritage--the old language and literature of Iceland--which our
miserably narrow scheme of education has hitherto defrauded them
of, it will have fulfilled its purpose.

HENRY SWEET
London,
February, 1886



GRAMMAR

1. This book deals with Old Icelandic in its classical period,
between 1200 and 1350.


PRONUNCIATION

2. The Icelandic alphabet was founded on the Latin, with the
addition of _脙戮_ and _脙掳_, and of the modified letters _脛聶_, _脟芦_,
_脙赂_, which last is in this book written _脙露_, _脟芦脤聢_.

Vowels

3. The vowel-letters had nearly the same values as in Old
English.  Long vowels were often marked by (脗麓).  In this book
long vowels are regularly marked by (脗炉)[1].  The following are
the elementary vowels and diphthongs, with examples, and
key-words from English, French (F.), and German (G.):--

[Footnote 1: Note that the longs of _脛聶_, _脙露_ are written _脙娄_,
_脜聯_, respectively.]

            a  _as in_  mann (G.)   halda (_hold_)
            脛聛     "     father      r脛聛脙掳 (_advice_)
            e     "     脙漏t脙漏 (F.)    gekk (_went_)
            脛聯[2]        . . .       l脛聯t (let _pret._)
            脛聶     "     men         m脛聶nn (_men_)

[Footnote 2: Where no keyword is given for a long vowel, its
sound is that of the corresponding short vowel lengthened.]

            脙娄  _as in_  there       s脙娄r (_sea_)
            i     "     fini (F.)   mikill (_great_)
            脛芦           . . .       l脛芦till (_little_)
            o     "     beau (F.)   or脙掳 (_word_)
            脜聧           . . .       t脜聧k (_look_)
            脟芦     "     not         h脟芦nd (_hand_)
            脙露     "     peu (F.)    k脙露mr (_comes_)
            脜聯           . . .       f脜聯ra (_bring_)
            脟芦脤聢     "     peur (F.)   g脟芦脤聢ra (_make_)
            u     "     sou (F.)    upp (_up_)
            脜芦           . . .       h脜芦s (_house_)
            y     "     tu (F.)     systir (_sister_)
            脠鲁           . . .       l脠鲁sa (_shine_)
            au    "     haus (G.)   lauss (_loose_)
            ei    =     脛聶 + i       bein (_bone_)
            ey    =     脛聶 + y       leysa (_loosen_)

4. The unaccented _i_ in _systir_, etc. (which is generally
written _e_ in the MSS.) probably had the sound of _y_ in _pity_,
which is really between _i_ and _e_.  The unacc. _u_ in _f脜聧ru_
(they went), etc. (which is generally written _o_ in the MSS.)
probably had the sound of _oo_ in _good_.

Note that several of the vowels go in pairs of _close_ and
_open_, thus:

                    close : e 脛聯 o 脜聧 脙露 脜聯
                    open  : 脛聶 脙娄 脟芦 - 脟芦脤聢 -

Consonants

5. Double consonants followed by a vowel must be pronounced
really double, as in Italian.  Thus the _kk_ in _drekka_ (to
drink) must be pronounced like the _kc_ in _bookcase_, while the
_k_ in _dr脛聶ki_ (dragon) is single, as in _booking_.  When final
(or followed by another cons.) double conss. are pronounced long,
as in _munn_ (mouth _acc._), _hamarr_ (hammer _nom._), _steinn_
(stone _nom._), distinguished from _mun_ (will _vb._), and the
accusatives _hamar_, _stein_.

6. _k_ and _g_ had a more front (palatal) sound before the front
vowels _e_, _脛聶_, _i_, _脙露_, _脟芦脤聢_, _y_, and their longs, as also
before _j_, as in _k脛聶nna_ (known), _keyra_ (drive), _g脟芦脤聢ra_
(make), _liggja_ (lie).

7. _kkj_, _ggj_ were probably pronounced simply as double front
_kk_, _gg_, the _j_ not being pronounced separately.

8. *f* had initially the sound of our _f_, medially and finally
that of _v_, as in _gefa_ (give), _gaf_ (gave), except of course
in such combinations as _ft_, where it had the sound of _f_.

9. *g* was a stopped (back or front--guttural or palatal) cons.
initially and in the combination _ng_, the two _g_'s in _ganga_
(go) being pronounced as in _go_.  It had the open sound of G.
_g_ in _sagen_ medially before the back vowels _a_, _o_, _脟芦_,
_u_, and all conss. except _j_, and finally:--_saga_ (tale),
_d脟芦gum_ (with days); _sag脙掳i_ (he said); _lag_ (he lay).  Before
the front vowels and _j_ it had the sound of G. _g_ in _liegen_,
or nearly that of _j_ (our _y_), as in _s脛聶gir_ (says), _s脛聶gja_
(to say).

10. Before voiceless conss. (_t_, _s_) _g_ seems to have been
pronounced _k_, as in _sagt_ (said), _dags_ (day's).

11. The _g_ was always sounded in the combination _ng_,
as in _single_, not as in _singer_.

12. *h* was sounded before _j_ in such words as _hjarta_ (heart)
much as in E. _hue_ (= hj脜芦).  _hl_, _hn_, _hr_, _hv_ probably
represented voiceless _l_, _n_, _r_, _w_ respectively, _hv_
being identical with E. _wh_: _hlaupa_ (leap), _hn脛芦ga_ (bend),
_hringr_ (ring), _hvat_ (what).

13. *j* is not distinguished from _i_ in the MSS.  It had the
sound of E. _y_ in _young_: _j脟芦r脙掳_ (earth), _s脛聶tja_ (to set).

14. *p* in _pt_ probably had the sound of _f_: _lopt_ (air).

15. *r* was always a strong point trill, as in Scotch.

16. *s* was always sharp.

17. *v* (which was sometimes written _u_ and _w_) had the sound
of E. _w_: _vel_ (well), _h脟芦ggva_ (hew).

18. *z* had the sound of _ts_: _b脛聶ztr_ (best).

19. *脙戮* and *脙掳* were used promiscuously in the older MS., the
very oldest using _脙戮_ almost exclusively.  In Modern Icelandic
_脙戮_ is written initially to express the sound of E. hard _th_,
_脙掳_ medially and finally to express that of soft _th_; as there
can be no doubt that this usage corresponds with the old
pronunciation, it is retained in this book: _脙戮ing_ (parliament),
_fa脙掳ir_ (father), _vi脙掳_ (against). In such combinations as _p脙掳_
the _脙掳_ must of course be pronounced _脙戮_.

Stress

20. The stress (accent) is always on the first syllable.


PHONOLOGY

Vowels

21. The vowels are related to one another in different ways, the
most important of which are _mutation_ (umlaut), _fracture_
(brechung), and _gradation_ (ablaut).

Mutation

22. The following changes are *i*-mutations (caused by an older
_i_ or _j_ following, which has generally been dropped)[3]:

[Footnote 3: Many of the _i_'s which appear in derivative and
inflectional syllables are late weakenings of _a_ and other
vowels, as in _bani_ (death) = Old English _bana_; these do not
cause mutation.]

*a* (*脟芦*) ... *脛聶* :-- _mann_ (man _acc._), _m脛聶nn_ (men); _h脟芦nd_
(hand), _h脛聶ndr_ (hands).

*脛聛* ... *脙娄* :-- _m脛聛l_ (speech), _m脙娄la_ (speak).

*e* (*ja*, *j脟芦*) ... *i* :-- _ver脙掳r_ (worth), _vir脙掳a_ (estimate).

*u* (*o*) ... *y* :-- _fullr_ (full), _fylla_ (to fill); _lopt_
(air), _lypta_ (lift).

*脜芦* ... *脠鲁* :-- _br脜芦n_ (eyebrow), pl. _br脠鲁nn_.

*o* ... *脙露* :-- _koma_ (to come), _k脙露mr_ (comes).

*脜聧* ... *脜聯* :-- _f脜聧r_ (went), _f脜聯ra_ (bring).

*au* ... *ey* :-- _lauss_ (loose), _leysa_ (loosen).

*j脜芦* (*j脜聧*) ... *脠鲁* :-- _sj脜芦kr_ (sick), _s脠鲁ki_ (sickness);
_lj脜聧sta_ (strike), _l脠鲁str_ (strikes).

23. The change of _a_ into _脛聶_ is sometimes the result of a
following _k_, _g_, or _ng_, as in _d脛聶gi_ dat. sg. of _dagr_
(day), _t脛聶kinn_ (taken), _g脛聶nginn_ (gone), inf. _taka_, _ganga_.
_i_ appears instead of _e_, and _u_ instead of _o_ before a nasal
followed by another cons.: cp. _binda_ (to bind), _bundinn_
(bound) with _bresta_ (burst) ptc. prt. _brostinn_.

24. There is also a *u*-mutation, caused by a following _u_,
which has often been dropped:

*a* ... *脟芦* :-- _dagr_ (day) dat. pl. _d脟芦gum_; _land_ (land) pl.
_l脟芦nd_.

25. Unaccented _脟芦_ becomes _u_, as in _sumur_ pl. of _sumar_
(summer), _k脟芦llu脙掳u_ (they called), infin. _kalla_.

Fracture

26. The only vowel that is affected by fracture is _e_: when
followed by original _a_ it becomes _ja_, when followed by
original _u_ it becomes _j脟芦_, as in _jar脙掳ar_ gen. of _j脟芦r脙掳_
(earth)[4].  When followed by original _i_, the _e_ is, of
course, mutated to _i_, as in _skildir_ plur. nom. of _skj脟芦ldr_
(shield), gen. _skjaldar_.

[Footnote 4: Cp. German _erde_.]

Gradation

27. By gradation the vowels are related as follows:--

*a* ... *脜聧* :-- _fara_ (go) pret. _f脜聧r_, whence by mut. _f脜聯ra_
(bring).

*e* (i, ja) ... *a* ... *u* (o) :-- _bresta_ (burst), prt.
_brast_, prt. pl. _brustu_, ptc. prt. _brostinn_; _finna_ (find),
_fundinn_ (found _ptc._), _fundr_ (meeting).

*e* ... *a* ... *脛聛* ... *o* :-- _stela_ (steal), prt. _stal_,
prt. pl. _st脛聛lu_, ptc. prt. _stolinn_.

*e* ... *a* ... *脛聛* ... *e* :-- _gefa_ (give), _gaf_ (he gave),
_g脛聛fu_ (they gave), _gefinn_ (given), _gj脟芦f_ (gift), _u_-fracture
of _gef-_, _g脙娄fa_ (luck) mut. of _g脛聛f-_.

*脛芦* ... *ei* ... *i* :-- _sk脛芦na_ (shine), _skein_ (he shone),
_skinu_ (they shone).  _s脜聧l-skin_ (sunshine).

*j脜芦* (j脜聧) ... *au* ... *u* ... *o* :-- _lj脜芦ga_ (tell a lie), prt.
_laug_, prt. pl. _lugu_, ptc. prt. _loginn_.  _lygi_ (lie _sbst._)
mut. of _lug-_.  _skj脜聧ta_ (shoot), _skj脜聧tr_ (swift), _skotinn_
(shot _ptc._), _skot_ (shot _subst._).

Other changes

28. All final vowels are long in accented syllables: _脙戮脛聛_ (then),
_n脜芦_ (now).

29. Inflectional and derivative vowels are often dropt after long
accented vowels: cp. _ganga_ (to go) with _f脛聛_ (to get), the dat.
plurals _knj脛聛m_ (knees) with _h脜芦sum_ (houses).

30. Vowels are often lengthened before _l_ + cons.: _h脛聛lfr_ (half
_adj._), _f脜聧lk_ (people); cp. _f脜聧lginn_ (hidden) with _brostinn_
(burst _ptc._).

Consonants

31. _v_ is dropped before _o_ and _u_: _vaxa_ (to grow), prt.
_脜聧x_, _vinna_ (to win), _unninn_ (won _ptc._), _svelta_ (to
starve), _soltinn_ (starved, hungry).

Final _r_ is often assimilated to a preceding cons.

32. _*-lr_, _*-nr_, _*-sr_ always become _-ll_, _-nn_, _-ss_
after a long vowel or diphthong, as in _st脜聧ll_ (chair _nom._),
acc. _st脜聧l_, _steinn_ (stone _nom._), acc. _stein_, _v脛芦ss_ (wise
_masc. nom. sg._), _v脛芦s_ fem. nom. sg., and in unacc. syllables,
as in the masc. sg. nominatives _mikill_ (great), fem. _mikil_,
_borinn_ (carried), fem.  _borin_, _脠鲁miss_ (various) fem. _脠鲁mis_.

33. Words in which _l_, _n_, _r_, _s_ are preceded by a cons.
drop the _r_ entirely, as in the masc. nominatives _jarl_ (earl),
_hrafn_ (raven), _vitr_ (wise), _脙戮urs_ (giant), _lax_ (salmon).

34. If _l_ and _n_ are preceded by a short accented vowel, the
_r_ is generally kept, as in _stelr_ (steals), _vinr_, (friend),
_sr_ becoming _ss_, as elsewhere.

35. _r_ is kept after _ll_, and generally after _nn_, as in the
masc. nom. _allr_ (all), and in _br脛聶nnr_ (burns).

36. _z_ often stands for _脙掳s_ as well as _ts_, as in _脙戮脛聯r
脙戮ykkizk_ (ye seem) = _*脙戮ykki脙掳-sk_, _Vest-firzkr_ (belonging to
the West Firths) = _-*fir脙掳skr_ (_f脟芦r脙掳r_, firth).

37. Inflectional _t_ is generally doubled after a long accented
vowel: _f脛聛r_ (few) neut. _f脛聛tt_ (cp. _allr_ 'all,' neut. _allt_),
_s脛聛_ (I saw), _s脛聛tt_ 'thou sawest.'


INFLECTIONS

Nouns

38. *Gender*.  There are three genders in Icelandic--masculine,
feminine, and neuter.  The gender is partly natural, partly
grammatical, generally agreeing with the gender in Old English.
Compound words follow the gender of their last element.

39. *Strong and Weak*.  All weak nouns end in a vowel in the nom.
sg. and in most of the other cases as well.  Most strong nouns
end in a cons. in the nom. sg.

40. *Cases*.  There are four cases--nominative, accusative,
dative, genitive.  All nouns (except a few contractions) have the
gen. pl. in _-a_ (_fiska_, of fishes), and the dat. pl. in _-um_
(_fiskum_).  All strong masculines (_fiskr_) and some strong
feminines (_br脜芦脙掳r_, bride) take _r_[5] in the nom. sg.  Most strong
feminines show the bare root in the nom. sg. with _u_-mutation,
if possible (_脛聛st_, favour, _f脟芦r_, journey).  The nom. pl. of all
strong masc. and fem. nouns ends in _r_ (_fiskar_, _脛聛stir_).  The
acc. pl. of fem. nouns is the same as the nom. pl. (_脛聛stir_).
The acc. pl. of masc. strong nouns always ends in a vowel
(_fiska_).  The plur. nom. and acc. of neuters is the same as the
sing. nom. and acc., except that in the plur. nom. and acc. they
take _u_-mutation, if possible (_h脜芦s_, houses, _l脟芦nd_, lands).

[Footnote 5: Subject, of course, to the assimilations described
above.]

41. The declensions are most conveniently distinguished by the
acc. plur.

                     Strong Masculines

                       (1) a-plurals

              SINGULAR                 PLURAL

      _Nom._  fisk-r (_fish_)          fisk-ar
      _Acc._  fisk                     fisk-a
      _Dat._  fisk-i                   fisk-um
      _Gen._  fisk-s                   fisk-a

42. So also _heimr_ (home, world); _konungr_ (king); _脙聻脜聧rr_
(Thor), acc. _脙聻脜聧r_, gen. _脙聻脜聧rs_; _steinn_ (stone), acc. _stein_,
gen. _steins_, pl. nom. _steinar_; _hrafn_ (raven), acc.
_hrafn_, pl. nom. _hrafnar_; _脙戮urs_ (giant), acc. gen. _脙戮urs_,
pl. nom. _脙戮ursar_.

43. Dissyllables in _-r_, _-l_, _-n_ generally throw out the
preceding vowel before a vowel-inflection: _hamarr_ (hammer),
dat. _hamri_; _j脟芦tunn_ (giant), pl. nom. _j脟芦tnar_.  _k脛聶till_
(kettle) and _lykill_ (key) show unmutated vowels in the
contracted forms, as in the acc. plur. _katla_, _lukla_.

44. Some nouns of this decl. take _-ar_ in the gen. sing.,
especially proper names, such as _H脛聛kon_, gen. _H脛聛konar_.

45. Some nouns add _v_ before vowels: _s脙娄r_ (sea), gen.
_s脙娄var_.

46. The dat. sometimes drops the _i_: _s脙娄_ (sea), _脙聻脜聧r_.  _dagr_
(day) mutates its vowel in the dat. _d脛聶gi_.

47. Nouns in _-ir_ keep the _i_ in the sing., and drop it in the
plur.:

              SINGULAR                 PLURAL

      _Nom._  h脛聶lli-r (_cave_)         h脛聶ll-ar
      _Acc._  h脛聶lli                    h脛聶ll-a
      _Dat._  h脛聶lli                    h脛聶ll-um
      _Gen._  h脛聶lli-s                  h脛聶ll-a

48. So also a number of proper names, such as _Skr脠鲁mir_, _脙聻脜聧rir_.

                        (2) i-plurals

              SINGULAR                 PLURAL

      _Nom._  sta脙掳-r (_place_)         sta脙掳-ir
      _Acc._  sta脙掳                     sta脙掳-i
      _Dat._  sta脙掳                     st脟芦脙掳-um
      _Gen._  sta脙掳-ar                  sta脙掳-a

49. So also _gripr_ (precious thing), _salr_ (hall).

50. _g脛聶str_ (guest) takes _-i_ in the dat. sg., and _-s_ in the
gen. sg.

51. Those ending in _g_ or _k_ (together with some others) insert
_j_ before _a_ and _u_: _b脛聶kkr_ (bench), _b脛聶kk_, _b脛聶kk_,
_b脛聶kkjar_; _b脛聶kkir_, _b脛聶kki_, _b脛聶kkjum_, _b脛聶kkja_.  So also
_m脛聶rgr_ (marrow), _str脛聶ngr_ (string).

                        (3) u-plurals

              SINGULAR                 PLURAL

      _Nom._  skj脟芦ld-r (_shield_)      skild-ir
      _Acc._  skj脟芦ld                   skj脟芦ld-u
      _Dat._  skild-i                  skj脟芦ld-um
      _Gen._  skjald-ar                skjald-a

52. So also _v脟芦ndr_ (twig), _v脟芦llr_ (plain), _vi脙掳r_ (wood).
_脛聛ss_ (god) has plur. nom. _脙娄sir_, acc. _脛聛su_.  _sonr_ (son) has
dat. sg. _syni_, plur. nom. _synir_.  It regularly drops its _r_
of the nom. in such compounds as _Tryggva-son_ (son of Tryggvi).

                        (4) r-plurals

              SINGULAR                 PLURAL

      _Nom._  f脜聧t-r (_foot_)           f脜聯t-r

Adjectives

83. Adjectives have three genders, and the same cases as nouns,
though with partly different endings, together with strong and
weak forms.

                     Strong Adjectives

                 MASC.             NEUT.        FEM.

   _Sg. Nom._    ung-r (_young_)   ung-t        ung
       _Acc._    ung-an            ung-t        ung-a
       _Dat._    ung-um            ung-u        ung-ri
       _Gen._    ung-s             ung-s        ung-rar

   _Pl. Nom._    ung-ir            ung          ung-ar
       _Acc._    ung-a             ung          ung-ar
       _Dat._    ung-um            ung-um       ung-um
       _Gen._    ung-ra            ung-ra       ung-ra

84. So also _fagr_ (fair), fem. _f脟芦gr_, neut. _fagrt_.

85. Some insert _j_ before _a_ and _u_: _n脠鲁r_ (new), _n脠鲁jum_,
_n脠鲁jan_.

86. Some insert _v_ before a vowel: _h脛聛r_ (high), _h脛聛van_,
_d脙露kkr_ (dark), _d脙露kkvir_, _kykr_ (alive), _kykvir_.

87. The _t_ of the neut. is doubled after a long vowel: _n脠鲁tt_,
_h脛聛tt_.  Monosyllables in _脙掳_, _dd_, _tt_ form their neut. in
_-tt_: _brei脙掳r_ (broad), _breitt_; _leiddr_ (led), _leitt_.
_g脜聧脙掳r_ (good) has neut. _gott_.  _sannr_ (true) has neut. _satt_.
In unaccented syllables or if a cons. precedes, _tt_ is shortened
to _t_: _kalla脙掳r_ (called), _kallat_; _blindr_ (blind), _blint_,
_har脙掳r_ (hard), _hart_, _fastr_ (firm), _fast_.

88. _l_ and _n_ assimilate a following _r_: _gamall_ (old), fem.
_g脟芦mul_, fem. acc. _gamla_, dat. _gamalli_. _v脟拢nn_ (beautiful),
gen.  pl. _v脙娄nna_.

Comparison

94. (1) with _-ari_, _-astr_: _r脛芦kr_ (powerful), _r脛芦kari_,
_r脛芦kastr_; _g脟芦fugr_ (distinguished), _g脟芦fgari_, _g脟芦fgastr_.

(young), _yngri_, _yngstr_.

104. _hundra脙掳_ is a strong neut.: _tvau hundru脙掳_ (240), _tveim

others weak adjectives.  _脙戮ri脙掳i_ inserts a _j_: _脙戮ri脙掳ja_, etc.

                           Definite

The prefixed definite article is declined thus:

117.

                 MASC.          NEUT.           FEM.

    _Sg. Nom._   inn            it              in
        _Acc._   inn            it              ina

        _Acc._   ina            in              inar
        _Dat._   inum           inum            inum
        _Gen._   inna           inna            inna

118. When suffixed to its noun it undergoes various changes. In
its monosyllabic forms it drops its vowel after a short
(un-accented) vowel, as in _auga-t_ (the eye), but keeps it after
a long vowel, as in _脛聛-in_ (the river), _tr脛聯-it_ (the tree).  The
dissyllabic forms drop their initial vowel almost everywhere;
not, however, after the _-ar_, _-r_, of the gen. sg., nor in
_m脛聶nninir_ (men, _nom._), _m脛聶nn-ina_ (men, _acc._).  The _-m_ of
the dat. pl. is dropped before the suffixed _-num_.

                           Relative

preceded by _s脛聛_: _s脛聛 er_ = he who, who, _s脜芦 er_ who fem.

Verbs

128. There are two classes of verbs, _strong_ and _weak_.  Strong
verbs are conjugated partly by means of gradation, weak verbs by
adding _脙掳_ (_d_, _t_).

129. The _脙掳_ of the 2 pl. is dropt before _脙戮it_ (ye two) and
_脙戮脛聯r_ (ye): _gefi 脙戮脛聯r_, _g脛聛fu 脙戮it_.

130. There is a middle voice, which ends in _-mk_ in the 1 pers.
sg. and pl., the rest of the verb being formed by adding _sk_ to
the active endings, _r_ being dropt, the resulting _ts_, _脙掳s_
being written _z_ (脗搂 36): _kvezk_ (active _kve脙掳r_ 'says'), _脙戮u
fekkzk_ (_fekkt_ 'gottest').

131. The following is the conjugation of the strong verb _gefa_
(give), which will show those endings which are common to all
verbs:

                            Active

                INDICATIVE          SUBJUNCTIVE

  _Present sg._ 1. gef              gef-a
                2. gef-r            gef-ir
                3. gef-r            gef-i

          _pl._ 1. gef-um           gef-im
                2. gef-i脙掳           gef-i脙掳
                3. gef-a            gef-i

_Preterite sg._ 1. gaf              g脙娄f-a
                2. gaf-t            g脙娄f-ir
                3. gaf              g脙娄f-i

          _pl._ 1. g脛聛f-um           g脙娄f-im
                2. g脛聛f-u脙掳           g脙娄f-i脙掳
                3. g脛聛f-u            g脙娄f-i

_Imperative sg._ 2 gef; _pl._ 1 gef-um, 2 gef-i脙掳.
_Participle pres._ gef-andi; _pret._ gef-inn.
_Infin._ gefa.

                            Middle

                INDICATIVE          SUBJUNCTIVE

    _Pres. sg._ 1. gef-umk          gef-umk
                2. gef-sk           gef-isk
                3. gef-sk           gef-isk

          _pl._ 1. gef-umk          gef-imk
                2. gef-izk          gef-izk
                3. gef-ask          gef-isk

    _Pret. sg._ 1. g脛聛f-umk          g脙娄f-umk
                2. gaf-zk           g脙娄f-isk
                3. gaf-sk           g脙娄f-isk

          _pl._ 1. g脛聛f-umk          g脙娄f-imk
                2. g脛聛f-uzk          g脙娄f-izk
                3. g脛聛f-usk          g脙娄f-isk

_Partic. pres._ gef-andisk; _pret._ gef-izk _neut._

                        Strong Verbs

132. In the strong verbs the plur. of the pret. indic. generally
has a different vowel from that of the sing.  The 1 sg. pret. of
the middle voice always has the vowel of the pl. pret.: _g脛聛fumk_.
The pret. subj. has the vowel of the pret. indic. plur. mutated:
_skaut_ (he shot), _skutu_ (they shot), _skyti_ (he might shoot).
But there is no mutation in verbs of the first conj.: _hlj脜聧pi_,
inf. _hlaupa_ (leap).

133. The pres. indic. sing. mutates the root-vowel in all three
persons: _ek sk脠鲁t_, _脙戮脜芦 sk脠鲁tr_, _hann sk脠鲁tr_, infin. _skj脜聧ta_
(shoot).  _e_ however is not mutated: _ek gef_, _脙戮脜芦 gefr_.  The
inflectional _r_ is liable to the same modifications as the _r_
of nouns (脗搂 32): _sk脛芦nn_, _v脛聶x_, infin. _sk脛芦na_ (shine), _vaxa_
(grow).

134. Verbs in _ld_ change the _d_ into _t_ in the 1, 3 sg. pret.
indic. and in the imper. sg.: _helt_ (held), _halt_ (hold!),
infin. _halda_.  _nd_ becomes _tt_, and _ng_ becomes _kk_ under
the same conditions: _binda_ (bind), _ganga_ (go), pret. _batt_,
_gekk_, imper. _bitt_, _gakk_.

135. The _t_ of the 2 sg. pret. indic. is doubled after a long
accented vowel: _脙戮脜芦 s脛聛tt_ (thou sawest).  If the 1 sg. pret.
indic. ends in _t_ or _脙掳_, the 2 sg. ends in _zt_: _l脛聯t_ (I let),
_脙戮脜芦 l脛聯zt_, _bau脙掳_ (I offered) _脙戮脜芦 bauzt_.

136. There are seven conjugations of strong verbs, distinguished
mainly by the characteristic vowels of their preterites.

                          Weak Verbs

150. There are three conjugations of weak verbs.  All those of
the first conjugation have mutated vowels in the pres., and form
their pret. with _脙掳_ (_d_, _t_): _heyra_ (hear), _heyr脙掳a_.  Those
of the second form their pret. in the same way, but have
unmutated vowels in the pres.: _hafa_ (have) _haf脙掳a_.  Those of
the third form their pret. in _-a脙掳a_: _kalla_ (call), _kalla脙掳a_.

                2. heyr-脙掳u脙掳         heyr-脙掳i脙掳

                    A. Without vowel-change

152. The inflectional _脙掳_ becomes _d_ after long syllables ending
in _l_ or _n_: _sigla_ (sail), _siglda_; _n脛聶fna_ (name),
_n脛聶fnda_, _n脛聶fndr_.

153. _-脙掳脙掳_ becomes _dd_: _lei脙掳a_ (lead), _leidda_.

154. _脙掳_ after _s_ and _t_ becomes _t_: _reisa_ (raise),
_reista_; _m脜聯ta_ (meet), _m脜聯tta_.  Also in a few verbs in _l_,
_n_: _m脙娄la_ (speak), _m脙娄lta_; _sp脛聶nna_ (buckle), _sp脛聶nta_.

155. After _nd_ and _pt_ it is dropped: _s脛聶nda_ (send), _s脛聶nda_,
_s脛聶ndr_; _lypta_ (lift), _lypta_.

156. It is preserved in such verbs as the following: _d脜聯ma_
(judge), _d脜聯m脙掳a_; _f脜聯ra_ (lead), _f脜聯r脙掳a_; _h脛聶r脙掳a_ (harden),
_h脛聶r脙掳a_; _hleypa_ (gallop), _hleyp脙掳a_.

                      B. With vowel-change

COMPOSITION

170. Composition with the genitive is very frequent in Icelandic.
Thus by the side of _skip-stj脜聧rn_ (ship-steering) we find
_skips-brot_ (ship's breaking, shipwreck), _skipa-h脛聶rr_ (army of
ships, fleet).  Genitival composition often expresses possession,
as in _konungs-skip_ (king's ship).


DERIVATION

Prefixes

171. Prefixes are much less used in Icelandic than in Old
English.

*al-* 'quite,' 'very': _al-b脜芦inn_ 'quite ready,' _al-snotr_ 'very
clever.'

*all-* 'all,' 'very': _all-valdr_ 'all-ruler, monarch,'
_all-har脙掳r_ 'very hard,' _all-st脜聧rum_ 'very greatly.'

*and-* 'against': _and-lit_ 'countenance' (_lita_, look),
_and-svar_ 'answer.'

*fj脟芦l-* 'many': _fj脟芦l-m脛聶nni_ 'multitude' (_ma脙掳r_, man).

*mis-* 'mis-': _mis-l脛芦ka_ 'displease.'

*脜芦-* 'un-': _脜芦-fri脙掳r_ 'war' (_fri脙掳r_, peace), _脜芦-happ_
'misfortune' (_happ_ luck).

Endings

                          (a) Nouns

                           Personal

172. *-ingr*, *-ingi*, *-ing*: _v脛芦kingr_ 'pirate,' _h脟芦f脙掳ingi_
'chief,' _k脛聶rling_ 'old woman.'

                           Abstract

173. *-脙掳*, fem. with mutation: _f脛聶gr脙掳_ 'beauty' (_fagr_, fair),
_f脛聶r脙掳_ 'journey' (_fara_, go), _l脛聶ng脙掳_ 'length' (_langr_, long).

*-ing*, fem.: _svipting_ 'pulling,' _v脛芦king_ 'piracy,' _vir脙掳ing_
'honour.'

*-leikr*, masc.: _k脜聯r-leikr_ 'affection' (_h脜聯rr_, dear),
_skj脜聧t-leikr_ 'speed' (_skj脜聧tr_, swift).

*-an*, *-un*, fem.: _skipan_ 'arrangement,' _sk脛聶mtun_
'amusement.'

                        (b) Adjectives

174. *-ugr*: _r脛聛脙掳ugr_ 'sagacious,' _脙戮r脜芦脙掳ugr_ 'strong.'

*-脜聧ttr*: _koll脜聧ttr_ 'bald,' _脟芦nd脜聧ttr_ 'fierce.'

*-lauss* '-less': _f脛聯-lauss_ 'moneyless,' _脜聧tta-lauss_ 'without
fear.'

*-ligr* '-ly': _undr-ligr_ 'wonderful,' _sann-ligr_ 'probable'
(_sannr_, true).

*-samr*: _l脛芦kn-samr_ 'gracious,' _skyn-samr_ 'intelligent.'

*-ver脙掳r* '-ward': _ofan-ver脙掳r_ 'upper.'

                          (c) Verbs

175. *-na*: _brotna_ 'be broken' (_brotinn_, broken), _hv脛芦tna_
'become white,' _vakna_ 'awake.'  Used to form intransitive and
inchoative verbs of the third conj.

                         (d) Adverbs

176. *-liga* '-ly': _undar-liga_ 'wonderfully,' _st脛聶rk-liga_
'strongly' (_st脛聶rkr_, strong).

*-um*, dat. pl.: _st脜聧rum_ 'greatly' (_st脜聧rr_, great).


SYNTAX

177. Icelandic syntax greatly resembles Old English, but has
several peculiarities of its own.

Concord

178. Concord is carried out very strictly in Icelandic: _allir
m脛聶nn v脛聛ru b脜芦nir_ 'all the men were ready,' _allir v脛聛ru drepnir_
'all were killed.'

179. A plural adj. or pronoun referring to two nouns of different
(natural or grammatical) gender is always put in the neuter: _脙戮脛聛
gekk hann upp, ok me脙掳 honum Loki_ (masc.), _ok 脙聻j脛聛lfi_ (masc.),
_ok R脟芦skva_ (fem.).  _脙戮脛聛 er 脙戮au_ (neut.) _h脟芦f脙掳u l脛芦tla hri脙掳
g脛聶ngit..._ 'he landed, and with him L., and 脙聻., and R.  When they
had walked for some time...'

Cases

180. The extensive use of the instrumental dative is very
characteristic of Icelandic: whenever the direct object of a verb
can be considered as the instrument of the action expressed by
the verb, it is put in the dative, as in _kasta spj脜聧ti_ 'throw a
spear' (lit. 'throw _with_ a spear'), _hann helt hamarskaptinu_
'he grasped the handle of the hammer,' _heita 脙戮v脛芦_ 'promise
that,' _j脛聛ta 脙戮v脛芦_ 'agree to that.'

Adjectives

181. The weak form of adjectives is used as in O.E. after the
definite article, _脙戮essi_ and other demonstratives.  _annarr_
(other) is always strong.

182., An adj. is often set in apposition to a following noun to
denote part of it: _eiga h脛聛lft d脠鲁rit_ 'to have half of the
animal,' _脟芦nnur 脙戮au_ 'the rest of them,' _of mi脙掳ja n脛聛tt_ 'in the
middle of the night.'

Pronouns

183. _s脛聛_ is often put pleonastically before the definite article
_inn_, both before and after the subst.: _s脛聛 inn ungi ma脙掳r_ 'that
young man,' _hafit 脙戮at it dj脜芦pa_ 'the deep sea.'

184. The definite article is generally not expressed at all, or
else _einn_, _einnhv脛聶rr_ is used.

185. A noun (often a proper name) is often put in apposition to a
dual pron. of the first and second persons, or a plur. of the
third person: _脙戮it f脛聯lagar_, 'thou and thy companions,' _me脙掳 脙戮eim
脛聙ka_ 'with him and 脛聙ki.'  Similarly _st脛聶ndr 脙聻脜聧rr upp ok 脙戮eir
f脛聯lagar_ 'Thor and his companions get up.'

186. The plurals _v脛聯r_, _脙戮脛聯r_ are sometimes used instead of the
singulars _ek_, _脙戮脜芦_, especially when a king is speaking or being
spoken to.

187. _sik_ and _s脛聯r_ are used in a strictly reflexive sense,
referring back to the subject of the sentence, like _se_ in
Latin: _脙聻orr bau脙掳 honum til matar me脙掳 s脛聯r_ 'Thor asked him to
supper with him.'

Verbs

188. The tenses for which there is no inflection in the active,
and all those of the passive, are formed by the auxiliaries
_skal_ (shall), _hafa_ (have), _vera_ (be) with the infin. and
ptc. pret., much as in modern English.

189. The historical present is much used, often alternating
abruptly with the preterite.

190. The middle voice is used: (1) in a purely reflexive sense:
_spara_ 'spare,' _sparask_ 'spare oneself, reserve one's
strength.'  (2) intransitively: _b脜芦a_ 'prepare,' _b脜芦ask_ 'become
ready, be ready'; _s脛聶tja_ 'set,' _s脛聶tjask_ 'sit down'; _s脠鲁na_
'show,' _s脠鲁nask_ 'appear, seem.'  (3) reciprocally: _b脛聶rja_
'strike,' _b脛聶rjask_ 'fight'; _hitta_, 'find,' _hittask_ 'meet.'
In other cases it specializes the meaning of the verb, often
emphasizing the idea of energy or effort: _koma_ 'come,' _komask_
'make one's way.'

191. The impersonal form of expression is widely used in
Icelandic: _rak 脛聛 storm_ (acc.) _fyrir 脙戮eim_ 'a storm was driven
in their face.'

192. The indef. 'one' is expressed in the same way by the third
pers. sg., and this form of expression is often used when the
subject is perfectly definite: _ok freista skal 脙戮essar 脛芦脙戮r脜聧ttar_
'and this feat shall be tried (by you).'

193. The abrupt change from the indirect to the direct narration
is very common: _Haraldi konungi var sagt at 脙戮ar var komit
bjarnd脠鲁ri, 'ok 脛聛 脛陋sl脛聶nzkr ma脙掳r,'_ 'King Harold was told that a
bear had arrived, and that an Icelander owned it.'  The direct
narration is also used after _at_ (that): _hann svarar at 'ek
skal r脛芦脙掳a til H脛聶ljar'_ 'he answers that he will ride to Hel.'

NOTES

The references marked Gr. are to the paragraphs of the Grammar.

I. THOR

Line 3. *Hann 脛聛 脙戮ar r脛芦ki er 脙聻r脜芦脙掳-vangar heita*, 'he reigns
(there) where it is called 脙聻.,' i.e. in the place which is called
脙聻.  The plur. _heita_ agrees with _脙戮r脜芦脙掳vangar_, as in l. 14
below: _脙戮at eru j脛聛rngl脜聧far_ 'that is (his) iron gloves.'

l. 5. *脙戮at er h脜芦s mest, sv脛聛 at m脛聶nn hafa g脟芦脤聢rt*, 'that is the
largest house, so that men have made (it),' i.e. the largest
house that has been built.  Note the plur. _h脜芦s_ of a single
house; each chamber was originally regarded as a house, being
often a detached building.

l. 13. *sp脛聶nnir 脙戮eim*, Gr. 脗搂 154; cp. 2. 49.


II. THOR AND 脜陋TGAR脙聬ALOKI

l. 1. *f脜聧r me脙掳 hafra s脛芦na...ok me脙掳 honum s脛聛, 脛聛ss er...*  We
see here that _me脙掳_ generally takes an acc. to denote passive,
and a dat. to denote voluntary accompaniment.

l. 5. *so脙掳it* refers to some such subst. as _sl脛聛tr_ (meat)
understood.

l. 11. *spr脛聶tti 脛聛...* _脛聛_ is here an adv.

l. 12. *til m脛聶rgjar.*  _til_ here implies intention--to get at
the marrow.

l. 20. *脙戮at er s脛聛 augnanna*, 'the little he saw of the eyes.'--
Thor frowned till his eyebrows nearly covered his eyes, and the
man felt as if he were going to fall down dead at the mere sight
of them.

l. 21. The second *hann* refers, of course, to Thor.

l. 34. *til myrkrs*, till it was dark.

l. 36. *脙戮eir*, the masc. instead of the neut. pl., as in l. 32
*foll.*, showing that _leitu脙掳u_ is meant to refer only to the men
of the party, and not to include R脟芦skva.  (Gr. 脗搂 179.)

l. 46. *s脛聯r hvar l脛聛 ma脙掳r*, 'saw where a man lay,' i.e. saw a man
lying.

l. 51. *einu sinni*, for once in his life.

l. 52. *n脛聶fndisk Skr脠鲁mir*, said his name was Skr.

l. 66. *b脜芦i脙掳 til* (_prp._) *n脛聛tt-ver脙掳ar y脙掳r*, prepare supper for
yourselves.

l. 77. *Er 脙戮at 脙戮脛聯r satt at s脛聶gja*.  _satt_ is in apposition to
_脙戮at_--'that is to be told you as the truth, (namely) that...'

l. 88. *sj脛聛 sik*, see himself alive.

l. 104. *脙戮ann* = _脙戮ann veg_, that way, course.

l. 108. *at 脙娄sirnir b脙娄脙掳i 脙戮脛聛 heila hittask*.  The full sense is,
'that Thor and Loki expressed a wish that they and Skr脠鲁mir might
meet again safe and sound.'

ll. 111, 112. *s脛聶ttu hnakkann 脛聛 bak s脛聯r aptr*, threw back the
backs of their heads till they touched their backs, i.e. threw
back their heads.

l. 118. *脜聯rit st脜聧ra*, 'rather big,' i.e. very big.

l. 120. *glotti um t脟芦nn*, 'grinned round a tooth,' i.e. showed
his teeth in a malicious grin.  Two MSS. read _vi脙掳_ instead of
_um_.

l. 121. *er annan veg en ek hygg, at...?*  is it otherwise than
as I think, namely that...?  i.e. am I not right in thinking
that...?

l. 127. *engi er h脛聯r s脛聛 inni er...* = engi er h脛聯r-inni s脛聛-er...

l. 129. *freista skal*, Gr. 脗搂 192.

l. 140. *kallar 脙戮ess meiri v脛聛n at hann s脛聯...*  'says that there
is more probability of that, namely that he is...than of the
contrary,' i.e. says that he will have to be...

l. 150. *f脜聧thvatari en sv脛聛*, 'more swift-footed than so--under
these circumstances,' i.e. than you.

l. 156. *ok er 脙聻j脛聛lfl eigi 脙戮脛聛 kominn...* = 脙戮脛聛 er 脙聻j脛聛lfi eigi
kominn...

l. 172. *at sinni*, this time.

l. 172. *hann*, acc.

l. 173. *laut 脜聧r horninu*, bent back from the horn.

l. 188. *mestr* refers to _drykkr_ understood.

l. 218. *kalli*, Gr. 脗搂 192.

l. 241. *脙戮脜聧* refers to _uni_.


III. BALDER

l. 7. *engi* agrees with _d脜聧mr_.


IV. THE DEATH OF BALDER

l. 11. *hann*, acc.

l. 20. *ungr*, too young.

l. 31. *脜芦-happ* is in apposition to _脙戮at_; cp. 3. 7.

ll. 33, 34. *v脛聛ru me脙掳 einum hug til...*  had the same feelings
towards.

l. 36. *var...fyrr*, was beforehand, prevented.

l. 42. *vili*, subj. 'whether he will';--change of construction.

l. 55. *nema*, 'unless,' here = 'until.'

l. 89. *heim*.  This use of _heim_ in the sense of 'someone
else's home.' is frequent.  Cp. our 'drive a nail home.'

l. 94. *sv脛聛* refers to _ok ef allir hlutir..._, the _ok_ being
pleonastic.

l. 108. *hvar*, cp. 2. 46.

l. 113. *karl*, 'old man,' here = Odin.


V. H脛聮脙聬INN AND HEGNI

l. 6. *H脛聯脙掳inn* = hann; this use of a proper name instead of a
pronoun is frequent.

l. 9. *脙戮ar*.  Cp. 1. 3.


VI. THE DEATH OF OLAF TRYGGVASON

l. 17. *sv脛聛 at*, so that, i.e. just when.

l. 30. *er*, namely that.

l. 33. *austan at sigla*, is in a kind of apposition to
_f脛聶r脙掳ina_.

l. 40. *sv脛聛*, also.

l. 48. *muni fyrir*, awaits you, is impending.

l. 53. *meira*, adv., better, faster.

l. 149. *bar hann h脛聛tt*, impers. w. acc.; he was in a conspicuous
place.

l. 244. *vi脙掳 fimt脛聛nda mann*, one of fifteen, with fourteen men.

l. 259. *v脛聛pna* is governed by the second half of the genitival
compound _kl脙娄脙掳a-b脜芦na脙掳_, which is here considered as two
independent words.


VII. AU脙聬UN

l. 17. *var fyrir*, was to be found.

l. 26. *tvau ver脙掳 sl脛芦k*, double the price you gave.

l. 55. *f脛聯* is probably dat. here, but may be nom.

l. 56. *脛聶ptir sem...*, according as, in accordance with what.

l. 64. *n脜芦...n脜芦*, lately...just now.

l. 116. *h脛聶ldr* is here used pleonastically in a kind of

l. 125. *en*, and = while.

l. 129. *脙戮essi einn var sv脛聛 hlutrinn, at...*, this single thing

VIII. 脙聻RYMSKVI脙聬A

l. 7. *jar脙掳ar* is governed by _hv脛聶rgi_.

l. 9. *t脜芦na*.  Poetical construction of gen. to denote goal of

l. 15. *脙戮脜聧* goes with the following _at_ = _ok s脛聶lja, 脙戮脜聧at_
(_脙戮脜聧tt_) _v脙娄ri 脜聧r silfri_.
